## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration typically depends on position x through nonlinear restoring forces, on velocity v through damping terms, and possibly on time t through external driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Combined quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general anharmonic potential)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving force)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametrically driven oscillator)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling term)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x**2 (comprehensive nonlinear model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential wells
- Even-power restoring forces (x²) break oscillation symmetry → asymmetric potential wells with drift
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping → limit cycle behavior (Van der Pol type)
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic driving → possible resonance and chaos
- Product terms x*v represent phase-space-dependent forces → energy-dependent dynamics and possible conservative nonlinear coupling
- Sinusoidal position dependence sin(c*x) suggests a periodic potential → pendulum-like large-amplitude behavior
- Parametric excitation appears as time-modulated coefficients of x → (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x indicating instability bands
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous system → phase portrait analysis and fixed-point classification apply
- Cubic velocity terms v³ indicate nonlinear drag → relevant for high-amplitude oscillations with fluid resistance
